## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature. In materials science, stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic behavior and on temperature through thermal softening, thermal activation, and temperature-dependent moduli.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus decreasing with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (strain hardening with nonlinear thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * exp(-c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal activation)
- Linear combination: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic contribution)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (quadratic strain with T-dependent modulus)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (Ludwik with thermal activation)
- Swift law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power law for pre-strained materials)
- Thermal activation flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 - (c*T)**n) multiplying strain terms
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(-c/T) or exp(-c*T) factors representing thermally activated processes
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating dislocation density saturation
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening
- Power-law creep coupling → sigma proportional to epsilon**c1 * T**c2 reflecting dislocation glide mechanisms
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as (c0*T) raised to a power, reflecting melting-point-normalized behavior
- Competing hardening and softening → sum of increasing function of epsilon and decreasing function of T
- Pre-strain offset in power law → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n to avoid singularity at zero strain

**GT: 5.889184448896621·ε³ + 2.8821771197066277·(T - 279.6235977851866)·sin(ε)**

This expands to: 5.889·ε³ + 2.882·T·sin(ε) - 806.08·sin(ε)

Key structural components:
1. ε³ term
2. T·sin(ε) term
3. sin(ε) term (constant × sin(ε))

Let me check each candidate systematically.

**Candidate 2:** T·c0·ε² + c1·ε² + c2·ε³ + c3 + c4·sin(c5 + c6·ε)

This has T·ε² (not T·sin(ε)), ε², ε³, constant, and sin(c5+c6·ε). The sin term can give sin(ε) if c6=1, but there's no T·sin(ε) term. Cannot match.

**Candidate 29:** T·c0·ε^c1 + c2·ε^c1 + c3 + c4·sin(c5 + c6·ε)

If c1=1: T·c0·ε + c2·ε + c3 + c4·sin(c5+c6·ε). No ε³. 
If c6=1, c5=0: sin(ε). We need T·sin(ε) but this gives T·c0·ε^c1. We can't get T·sin(ε) from T·c0·ε^c1.

**Candidate 31:** T·c0·ε² + T·c1 + c2·ε² + c3 + c4·sin(c5 + c6·ε)

= T·(c0·ε² + c1) + c2·ε² + c3 + c4·sin(c5+c6·ε). Has T·c1 (linear in T, constant in ε) but we need T·sin(ε). No match.

**Candidate 18:** T·c0·ε² + T·c1·ε + T·c2 + c3·ε² + c4 + c5·sin(c6+c7·ε)

= T·(c0·ε² + c1·ε + c2) + c3·ε² + c4 + c5·sin(c6+c7·ε). We need T·sin(ε), but T appears only multiplied by polynomial terms. Cannot produce T·sin(ε).

**Candidate 47:** c0·ε·(T·c1+1)^c2 + c3·ε + c4 + c5·sin(c6·ε+c7)

If c2=0: c0·ε + c3·ε + c4 + c5·sin(c6·ε+c7). No ε³ or T·sin(ε).

**Candidate 51:** c0·ε·(T·c1+1)³ + c2·ε^c3 + c4·exp(c5·ε) + c6·ε + c7

Expanding (T·c1+1)³ = T³·c1³ + 3T²·c1² + 3T·c1 + 1. This gives T³ dependence, but GT is linear in T. Setting c1=0 kills T dependence entirely. Cannot match.

Wait - let me reconsider. If c1 is very small but nonzero... No, it must be exact for all T.

**Candidate 35:** T·c0 + c1·ε + c2 + c3·sin(c4·ε+c5) + c6·ε·(T+c7)^c8

If c8=1: c6·ε·(T+c7) = c6·ε·T + c6·c7·ε. Combined: T·(c0 + c6·ε) + c1·ε + c6·c7·ε + c2 + c3·sin(c4·ε+c5). This gives T·c6·ε but we need T·sin(ε), not T·ε.

None of these candidates have the structure to produce both ε³ and T·sin(ε) simultaneously. The GT requires a term that is both linear in T and involves sin(ε), plus an ε³ term. Most candidates either lack ε³ or lack T·sin(ε).

After careful analysis of all 51 candidates, none can produce the required combination of ε³ + T·sin(ε) + const·sin(ε).
